class="firstHeading" lang="en">Robbie Williams</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vcard plainlist" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: Records">Chrysalis</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap">Associated acts</span></th><td>\n<div class="hlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gary_Barlow" title="Gary Barlow">Gary Barlow</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://robbiewilliams.com">robbiewilliams<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Robert Peter</b> <b>Williams</b> (born 13 February 1974) is an English singer-songwriter and entertainer. He was a member of the pop group <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a> from 1990 to 1995 and again from 2009 to 2012. He has also had commercial success as a solo artist.\n</p><p>Williams rose to fame in Take That\'s first run in the early-to-mid-1990s. After many disagreements with the management and group members, Williams left the group in 1995 to launch a solo career, in which all but one of his 11 studio albums have reached <a href="/wiki/List_of_artists_by_number_of_UK_Albums_Chart_number_ones" title="List of artists by number of UK Albums Chart number ones">number one</a> in the UK. Williams also released seven number-one singles.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> On 15 July 2010, he rejoined Take That. The group\'s subsequent album <i><a href="/wiki/Progress_(Take_That_album)" title="Progress (Take That album)">Progress</a></i> became the second fastest-selling album in UK chart history<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and the fastest-selling record of the century at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Barlow" title="Gary Barlow">Gary Barlow</a> has since confirmed that Williams had left for a second time, although the departure was amicable and that Williams was welcome to rejoin Take That in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He is the best-selling British solo artist in the United Kingdom and the best selling non-Latino artist in Latin America. Six of his albums are among the top 100 biggest-selling albums in the United Kingdom\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of best-selling albums in the United Kingdom">four albums in the top 60</a>\xe2\x80\x93and in 2006 he entered the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Book of World Records">Guinness Book of World Records</a></i> for selling 1.6 million tickets of his <a href="/wiki/Close_Encounters_Tour" title="Close Encounters Tour">Close Encounters Tour</a> in a single day.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Williams has received a record eighteen <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a>\xe2\x80\x94winning Best British Male four times, and two awards for Outstanding Contribution to Music and the 2017 Brits Icon for his "lasting impact on <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British culture</a>", twelve German <a href="/wiki/ECHO_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="ECHO Awards">ECHO Awards</a>, and three <a href="/wiki/MTV_European_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV European Music Awards">MTV European Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brits_Icon_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brits_Icon-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brits_Winners_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brits_Winners-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, he was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> after being voted the "Greatest Artist of the 1990s". According to the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI), Williams has been certified for 19.8 million albums and 6.6 million singles in the UK as a solo artist.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He is also one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling music artists of all time</a>, having sold 75 million records worldwide. Williams also topped the 2000\xe2\x80\x932010 UK airplay chart, racking up almost 50% more plays than the <a href="/wiki/Sugababes" title="Sugababes">Sugababes</a> at number 2. In 2014, he was awarded the freedom of his home town of <a href="/wiki/Stoke-on-Trent" title="Stoke-on-Trent">Stoke-on-Trent</a>, as well as having a tourist trail created and streets named in his honour.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" nominations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Discography"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Discography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Tours"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Tours</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Robbie_Williams_band"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Robbie Williams band</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Timeline"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Timeline</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>\n<p>Williams was born on 13 February 1974 in <a href="/wiki/Stoke-on-Trent" title="Stoke-on-Trent">Stoke-on-Trent</a>, Staffordshire, England. His parents, Janet (<i><a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9e" class="mw-redirect" title="N\xc3\xa9e">n\xc3\xa9e</a></i> Farrell) and Peter Williams (also known as Pete Conway), ran a pub called the Red Lion in <a href="/wiki/Burslem" title="Burslem">Burslem</a>, before his father became the licensee at the <a href="/wiki/Port_Vale_F.C." title="Port Vale F.C.">Port Vale FC</a> Social Club; this led to Williams\' lifelong affinity for the team.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His maternal grandfather was Irish and hailed from <a href="/wiki/Kilkenny" title="Kilkenny">Kilkenny</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Williams attended <a href="/wiki/St_Margaret_Ward_Catholic_School" class="mw-redirect" title="St Margaret Ward Catholic School">St Margaret Ward Catholic School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tunstall,_Staffordshire" title="Tunstall, Staffordshire">Tunstall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> before attending dance school UKDDF in Tunstall. He participated in several school plays, and his biggest role was that of the <a href="/wiki/Artful_Dodger" title="Artful Dodger">Artful Dodger</a> in a production of <i><a href="/wiki/Oliver!" title="Oliver!">Oliver!</a></i>, the musical adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> novel <i><a href="/wiki/Oliver_Twist" title="Oliver Twist">Oliver Twist</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Take_That">Take That</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a></div>\n<h3><span id="1990.E2.80.931995:_first_stint"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1990\xe2\x80\x931995:_first_stint">1990\xe2\x80\x931995: first stint</span></h3>\n<p>In 1990, the sixteen-year-old Williams was the youngest member to join Take That. According to the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Take_That:_For_the_Record" title="Take That: For the Record">Take That: For the Record</a></i>, his mother read an advertisement seeking members for a new boy band and suggested that he try out for the group. He met fellow member <a href="/wiki/Mark_Owen" title="Mark Owen">Mark Owen</a> on the day of his audition/interview with <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Martin-Smith" title="Nigel Martin-Smith">Nigel Martin-Smith</a>. During the heights of the band\'s popularity, Williams was known as the extrovert and cheeky practical joker of the band. Although the majority of the band\'s material was written and performed by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Barlow" title="Gary Barlow">Gary Barlow</a>, Williams did perform lead vocals on their first Top Ten hit "<a href="/wiki/Could_It_Be_Magic" title="Could It Be Magic">Could It Be Magic</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Found_Heaven" title="I Found Heaven">I Found Heaven</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Everything_Changes_(Take_That_song)" title="Everything Changes (Take That song)">Everything Changes</a>". However, he had conflicts with Martin-Smith over the restrictive rules for Take That members, and he began drinking more <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcohol</a> and dabbling in <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 1994, Williams\'s drug abuse had escalated to the point of his having a near drug overdose the night before the group was scheduled to perform at the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Robbie_Williams_early_career_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robbie_Williams_early_career-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> According to the documentary <i>For the Record</i>, he stated that he was unhappy with his musical ideas not being taken seriously by lead singer Barlow and Martin-Smith, because his desire to explore <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rap_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap (music)">rap</a> conflicted with the band\'s usual ballads. Barlow explained in interviews that Williams had given up trying to offer creative input and merely did as he was told. As well as Williams\'s friction with the management of the band, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Orange" title="Jason Orange">Jason Orange</a> had problems with his increasingly belligerent behaviour, his lack of interest in performing, and his frequent habit of missing the band\'s rehearsals.\n</p><p>Both Orange and Barlow confronted Martin-Smith about the internal conflict, because they did not want him dropping out while touring and before any possible future touring of America, which never took place. During one of the last rehearsals before the tour commenced, the group confronted Williams about his attitude and stated they wanted to do the tour without him. He agreed to quit and left the group in July 1995; it would be the last time for twelve years that they were all together. Despite the departure of Williams, Take That completed their <a href="/wiki/Nobody_Else_Tour" title="Nobody Else Tour">Nobody Else Tour</a> as a four-piece band. They later disbanded on 13 February 1996, Williams\'s 22nd birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shortly afterwards, Williams was photographed by the press partying with the members of <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a> at <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a>. Following his departure, he became the subject of talk shows and newspapers as he acknowledged his plans to become a solo singer, and he was spotted partying with <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a> in France. However, a clause in his Take That contract prohibited him from releasing any material until after the group was officially dissolved, and he was later sued by Martin-Smith and forced to pay $200,000 in commission. After various legal battles over his right to a solo career, Williams was victorious in getting released from his contract with <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann_Music_Group" title="Bertelsmann Music Group">BMG</a>. On 27 June 1996, Williams signed with <a href="/wiki/Chrysalis_Records" title="Chrysalis Records">Chrysalis Records</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.93present:_second_stint"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009\xe2\x80\x93present:_second_stint">2009\xe2\x80\x93present: second stint</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg/210px-Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg" width="210" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg/315px-Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg/420px-Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1121" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_Williams_at_Sunderland_2011a_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams performing in Take That\xe2\x80\x99s <a href="/wiki/Progress_Live" title="Progress Live">Progress Live</a> tour in 2011. He rejoined the group in July 2010 and is open to another reunion in the future.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 27 March 2009, Williams stated he felt ready to re-join <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a>. He said: "I\'m in regular contact with them, even Gaz, and it\'s looking more likely by the week. The lads all seem up for it and some people think it\'s a done deal. I think it would be fun."<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Williams was eager to re-join the band on their <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Live" class="mw-redirect" title="The Circus Live">The Circus Live</a> tour, but these plans never materialised. In September 2009, Williams was reported to be working in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> with Take That, however these rumours were never confirmed.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While it was rumoured that Williams would reunite with Take That on 12 November 2009 for a <a href="/wiki/Children_in_Need" title="Children in Need">Children in Need</a> charity concert at <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Albert_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="The Royal Albert Hall">The Royal Albert Hall</a>, they merely greeted each other warmly on stage between performances. However, both did join with the other acts in the final song of the evening, with Williams putting his arm around Gary Barlow and singing "<a href="/wiki/Hey_Jude" title="Hey Jude">Hey Jude</a>".\n</p><p>On 15 July 2010, Williams rejoined Take That. In November 2010 the Take That album <i><a href="/wiki/Progress_(Take_That_album)" title="Progress (Take That album)">Progress</a></i> was released, becoming the fastest selling album since 2000 and the second fastest selling album in UK history. Williams explained that the long-standing feud between himself and Gary has been resolved, and how close they now were.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The band also announced the <a href="/wiki/Progress_Live" title="Progress Live">Progress Live</a> tour which would travel across the UK, including a record breaking 8 nights at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> in London,<sup id="cite_ref-wembleystadium.com_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wembleystadium.com-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> then continue across Europe. The tour was the fastest selling in UK history with ticket hotlines and websites crashing under the demand.<sup id="cite_ref-wembleystadium.com_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wembleystadium.com-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2012, Take That performed at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>. Williams was due to perform with the band but dropped out due to his wife giving birth at around the same time and thus the group performed as a four-piece.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Due to his solo-career commitments, Williams chose not to return for Take That\'s <a href="/wiki/III_(Take_That_album)" title="III (Take That album)">seventh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wonderland_(Take_That_album)" title="Wonderland (Take That album)">eighth</a> studio albums and their accompanying tours. Despite his absence, Gary Barlow still considers Williams part of the band, stating that "the band is for us all to come and go and we please."<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Williams continues to write music with his bandmates and has performed with the band on several occasions since 2011\'s Progress tour<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and plans on returning for a full tour to celebrate Take That\'s 25th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_career">Solo career</span></h2>\n<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.931998:_Life_thru_a_Lens_and_I.27ve_Been_Expecting_You"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996\xe2\x80\x931998:_Life_thru_a_Lens_and_I\'ve_Been_Expecting_You">1996\xe2\x80\x931998: <i>Life thru a Lens</i> and <i>I\'ve Been Expecting You</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Life_thru_a_Lens" title="Life thru a Lens">Life thru a Lens</a> and <a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Been_Expecting_You" title="I&#39;ve Been Expecting You">I\'ve Been Expecting You</a></div>\n<p>After leaving Take That, Williams launched his solo career starting off in 1996 by covering <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Freedom_(Robbie_Williams_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom (Robbie Williams song)">Freedom</a>", the single reached number two in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8notes_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8notes-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Recordings for Williams\'s first album began at London\'s Maison Rouge studios in March 1997. Shortly after his introduction to <a href="/wiki/Guy_Chambers" title="Guy Chambers">Guy Chambers</a>, Williams released "<a href="/wiki/Old_Before_I_Die" title="Old Before I Die">Old Before I Die</a>" which would be the first single taken from his debut album. The single reached number two on the UK Charts;<sup id="cite_ref-8notes_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8notes-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> however, it was largely ignored on international charts. His debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Life_thru_a_Lens" title="Life thru a Lens">Life thru a Lens</a></i>, was released in September 1997. The album launched with his first live solo gig at the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lys%C3%A9e_Montmartre" title="\xc3\x89lys\xc3\xa9e Montmartre">\xc3\x89lys\xc3\xa9e Montmartre</a> theatre in Paris, France. The album debuted at number eleven on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>.\n</p><p>Williams released what would be the fourth single taken from his album. "Angels" became Williams\' best-seller in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-BPI_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The song, apart from becoming a hit around Europe and Latin America, caused sales of his album to skyrocket. The album remained inside the British top ten for forty weeks and spent 218 weeks there altogether, making it the 58th best selling album in UK history with sales of over 2.4&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The album eventually managed to sell over three million copies in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-ifpi2002_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ifpi2002-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Williams and Chambers started writing the second album in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> in early 1998. The first single, "<a href="/wiki/Millennium_(single)" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium (single)">Millennium</a>", accompanied with a music video featuring Williams parodying <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a>, complete with <a href="/wiki/Tuxedo" title="Tuxedo">tuxedo</a> and references to Bond films like <i><a href="/wiki/Thunderball_(film)" title="Thunderball (film)">Thunderball</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/From_Russia_with_Love_(film)" title="From Russia with Love (film)">From Russia with Love</a></i>, became Williams\' first solo number one single in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-UK_Top_40_Database_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Top_40_Database-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> It also became a top twenty hit in many European countries, Latin America and Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When the album <i><a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Been_Expecting_You" title="I&#39;ve Been Expecting You">I\'ve Been Expecting You</a></i> was released in late October 1998, it debuted at number one in the UK Albums Chart.<sup id="cite_ref-UK_Top_40_Database_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Top_40_Database-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The album received more attention outside the United Kingdom, leaving its mark in the European and Latin American markets with hits such as "<a href="/wiki/No_Regrets_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="No Regrets (Robbie Williams song)">No Regrets</a>", a collaboration with The <a href="/wiki/Pet_Shop_Boys" title="Pet Shop Boys">Pet Shop Boys</a>\' singer <a href="/wiki/Neil_Tennant" title="Neil Tennant">Neil Tennant</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Divine_Comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="The Divine Comedy">The Divine Comedy</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Neil_Hannon" title="Neil Hannon">Neil Hannon</a>. A cover of a track from <a href="/wiki/World_Party" title="World Party">World Party</a>\'s album, <i>Egyptology</i>, became Williams\' second number one hit in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-UK_Top_40_Database_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Top_40_Database-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Williams finished the year with a European Tour late in 1999. The album <i>I\'ve Been Expecting You</i> sold almost 3&#160;million copies in the UK and was certified 10x Platinum by the BPI.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In Europe, the album sold over 4&#160;million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1999.E2.80.932001:_Sing_When_You.27re_Winning_and_Swing_When_You.27re_Winning"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999\xe2\x80\x932001:_Sing_When_You\'re_Winning_and_Swing_When_You\'re_Winning">1999\xe2\x80\x932001: <i>Sing When You\'re Winning</i> and <i>Swing When You\'re Winning</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Ego_Has_Landed" title="The Ego Has Landed">The Ego Has Landed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sing_When_You%27re_Winning" title="Sing When You&#39;re Winning">Sing When You\'re Winning</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swing_When_You%27re_Winning" title="Swing When You&#39;re Winning">Swing When You\'re Winning</a></div>\n<p>In 1999, Williams was signed to <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a> in the United States, a part of <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>. He embarked on a United States promotional tour and released his first United States and Canadian single, "<a href="/wiki/Millennium_(song)" title="Millennium (song)">Millennium</a>". The album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ego_Has_Landed" title="The Ego Has Landed">The Ego Has Landed</a></i> was released in July 1999 in the United States and Canada. In the middle of promotion and the tours in 1999, Williams began work on his third studio album. This time he had finally found his inner confidence.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg/220px-Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg/330px-Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg/440px-Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2953" data-file-height="2020" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_paparazzi_V_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams in London in 2000, <a href="/wiki/V_sign#V_sign_as_an_insult" title="V sign">gesturing</a> to a paparazzi photographer</div></div></div>\n<p>The first single taken from the album was "<a href="/wiki/Rock_DJ_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock DJ (song)">Rock DJ</a>", a song inspired by Williams\'s <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> mentor, the late <a href="/wiki/Ian_Dury" title="Ian Dury">Ian Dury</a>. The video created by Fred &amp; Farid<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> showed Williams in an attempt to get noticed by a group of females, first stripping and then tearing chunks of skin and muscle from his body, and caused controversy in the United Kingdom and many other countries. The video was edited by <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i> for its graphic content and many other channels followed suit.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The song became an instant hit, reaching number one in the UK (becoming his third number one single as a solo artist) and New Zealand. The song went on to win "Best Song of 2000" at the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>, "Best Single of the Year" at the <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a> and an <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Special_Effects" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Special Effects">MTV Video Music Award for Best Special Effects</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When the album, <i><a href="/wiki/Sing_When_You%27re_Winning" title="Sing When You&#39;re Winning">Sing When You\'re Winning</a></i> was released in August 2000, it topped the charts in many different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In the UK the album was certified 2x Platinum on its first week of release.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> After the success of his third album, Williams wanted to take another musical direction. He took two weeks off from his tour to record <i><a href="/wiki/Swing_When_You%27re_Winning" title="Swing When You&#39;re Winning">Swing When You\'re Winning</a></i>, his fourth studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Born from his lifelong love for <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;combined with the success of the track "<a href="/wiki/Have_You_Met_Miss_Jones%3F" title="Have You Met Miss Jones?">Have You Met Miss Jones?</a>" that he recorded for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Bridget_Jones%27s_Diary_(film)" title="Bridget Jones&#39;s Diary (film)">Bridget Jones\' Diary</a></i> in 2001&#160;&#8211;&#32;the album was recorded at <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Studios" title="Capitol Studios">Capitol Studios</a> in Los Angeles.\n</p><p>Williams took the chance to duet with his long-time friend <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Wilkes" title="Jonathan Wilkes">Jonathan Wilkes</a>, <i>Little Voice</i> star <a href="/wiki/Jane_Horrocks" title="Jane Horrocks">Jane Horrocks</a>, <i>Saturday Night Live</i> star <a href="/wiki/Jon_Lovitz" title="Jon Lovitz">Jon Lovitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Everett" title="Rupert Everett">Rupert Everett</a> and actress <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman" title="Nicole Kidman">Nicole Kidman</a>. The first single released from the album was a duet with Kidman, on "<a href="/wiki/Somethin%27_Stupid" title="Somethin&#39; Stupid">Somethin\' Stupid</a>". Originally a hit for <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Sinatra" title="Nancy Sinatra">Nancy Sinatra</a>, the song became Williams\' fifth number one hit in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> It eventually went on to become one of the biggest hits of 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> "Beyond the Sea" was featured over the credits of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo">Finding Nemo</a></i> in 2003 and was also released on the film\'s soundtrack CD. A DVD, <i>Robbie Williams Live at the Albert Hall</i>, was released in December of that year. So far, it has become one of the best selling music DVDs in Europe, being certified 6x Platinum in the United Kingdom<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and 2x Platinum in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2002.E2.80.932005:_Escapology_and_Intensive_Care"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002\xe2\x80\x932005:_Escapology_and_Intensive_Care">2002\xe2\x80\x932005: <i>Escapology</i> and <i>Intensive Care</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Escapology_(album)" title="Escapology (album)">Escapology (album)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Robbie_Williams_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Robbie Williams album)">Greatest Hits (Robbie Williams album)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Intensive_Care_(album)" title="Intensive Care (album)">Intensive Care (album)</a></div>\n<p>In 2002, Williams signed a record-breaking \xc2\xa380&#160;million contract with EMI.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The contract included a number of provisos, including the label ceding greater creative control to the artist and a commitment to breaking Williams into the US market. So far it is the biggest music deal in British history. The deal was brokered by <a href="/wiki/Ingenious_Media" title="Ingenious Media">Ingenious Media</a>, a leading UK corporate finance advisory business.<sup id="cite_ref-robbiewilliams_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robbiewilliams-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Williams began working on what would be his fifth studio album, spending a year in the recording studio. The album heralded a new era for Williams. He had taken a more active role in the making of this album, giving an indication of his growing confidence in the studio.  "One Fine Day", "Nan\'s Song", and "<a href="/wiki/Come_Undone_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Come Undone (Robbie Williams song)">Come Undone</a>" were the first songs that Williams wrote without the input of Guy Chambers. Most of the songs were recorded in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-robbiewilliams_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robbiewilliams-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:27%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x9cFor the first time in my life, I\'m speechless.\xe2\x80\x9d</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Williams addresses the crowd during his three record-breaking <a href="/wiki/Concerts_at_Knebworth_House" title="Concerts at Knebworth House">concerts at Knebworth</a> playing to 375,000, the biggest event in UK music history.<sup id="cite_ref-Knebworth_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knebworth-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The album\'s first single, "<a href="/wiki/Feel_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Feel (Robbie Williams song)">Feel</a>", written by Williams and Chambers, was recorded as a demo. When they started working on the album and were trying to re-record the vocals, Williams felt unsatisfied with it, so he decided to include the demo version and then release it as the first single.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> When the single was released in late 2002, it became Williams\' biggest international hit, going number one in countries like The Netherlands and Italy, as well as reaching the top ten in almost every single European country.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> When Williams\' fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Escapology_(album)" title="Escapology (album)">Escapology</a></i>, was released in late 2002, it hit number one in at least 10 countries around the world. In the United States, however, it failed to make such an impact. <i>Escapology</i> sold almost 2&#160;million copies by the end of 2003 in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On 1\xe2\x80\x933 August 2003, Williams played three consecutive <a href="/wiki/Concerts_at_Knebworth_House" title="Concerts at Knebworth House">concerts at Knebworth</a> to 125,000 people each night, making it the biggest event in UK music history.<sup id="cite_ref-Knebworth_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knebworth-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Memorable performances included \xe2\x80\x9cCome Undone\xe2\x80\x9d where he interjected with \xe2\x80\x9cBritain, I\xe2\x80\x99m Your Son\xe2\x80\x9d, and further interacted with the audience when he brought a girl up on stage.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In October 2003, Williams released a live album of the concerts, <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Knebworth" title="Live at Knebworth">Live at Knebworth</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2004, Williams released, <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Robbie_Williams_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Robbie Williams album)">Greatest Hits</a></i>, a retrospective of his career, and also, to reveal the new tracks he had been working on with the then-new collaborator, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Duffy" title="Stephen Duffy">Stephen Duffy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-robbiewilliams2_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robbiewilliams2-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Radio_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Radio (Robbie Williams song)">Radio</a>", the compilation\'s first single, debuted at number one in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a><sup id="cite_ref-UK_Top_40_Database_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Top_40_Database-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> (becoming Williams\' sixth number-one hit). When the compilation was later released it debuted at number one in the UK<sup id="cite_ref-UK_Top_40_Database_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_Top_40_Database-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and was the best selling album of the year in the UK<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline.co.uk_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline.co.uk-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Eight years after the release of "Angels", the British public voted it as the "Best Single of the Past Twenty-Five Years" at the <a href="/wiki/2005_Brit_Awards" title="2005 Brit Awards">2005 Brit Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After touring Latin America in late 2004 for the promotion <i>Greatest Hits</i>, Williams started working on his sixth studio album. Recorded at his house in the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Hills" title="Hollywood Hills">Hollywood Hills</a>, the album was co-written by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Duffy" title="Stephen Duffy">Stephen Duffy</a> over the course of 24 months.<sup id="cite_ref-robbiewilliams3_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robbiewilliams3-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The album <i><a href="/wiki/Intensive_Care_(album)" title="Intensive Care (album)">Intensive Care</a></i> was launched in Berlin on 9 October. It became a smash hit around the world. In November 2005, Williams took home the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Award</a> for \'Best Male\', but also, entered in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="The Guinness Book of World Records">The Guinness Book of World Records</a></i> when he announced his World Tour for 2006, selling 1.6&#160;million tickets in one single day.<sup id="cite_ref-sp-13394_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sp-13394-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Williams kicked off his <i><a href="/wiki/Close_Encounters_Tour" title="Close Encounters Tour">Close Encounters World Tour</a></i> in South Africa in April 2006, when he finished his European leg of the tour. 2.5&#160;million people had seen the show, and after touring Latin America and Australia the numbers went up to 3&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2006.E2.80.932009:_Rudebox_and_Reality_Killed_the_Video_Star"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006\xe2\x80\x932009:_Rudebox_and_Reality_Killed_the_Video_Star">2006\xe2\x80\x932009: <i>Rudebox</i> and <i>Reality Killed the Video Star</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Rudebox" title="Rudebox">Rudebox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reality_Killed_the_Video_Star" title="Reality Killed the Video Star">Reality Killed the Video Star</a></div>\n<p>Williams released his much anticipated dance/electro album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rudebox_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rudebox (album)">Rudebox</a></i>, on 23 October 2006. It featured collaborations with the <a href="/wiki/Pet_Shop_Boys" title="Pet Shop Boys">Pet Shop Boys</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a>, Soul Mekanik, <a href="/wiki/Joey_Negro" class="mw-redirect" title="Joey Negro">Joey Negro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a>, Chris Grierson, and The Orr Boys. It received mixed reviews: Allmusic gave it a four star rating, the <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> 8 out of 10, and Music Week and MOJO were equally positive,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> but it received much weaker reviews from some of the British press. The album sold 2x Platinum in Europe with sales of over 2&#160;million making it the fastest platinum-selling album of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> To promote his album, Williams commissioned a series of short films.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <i>Goodbye to the Normals</i> was directed by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Field_Smith" title="Jim Field Smith">Jim Field Smith</a> and features "Burslem Normals" by Williams.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg/170px-Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg/255px-Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg/340px-Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="638" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_Williams_catzi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams at a concert in Vienna, Austria in 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>Rumours of a new studio album co-written with Guy Chambers surfaced in early 2007, along with known commitments required by Williams to his EMI contract. British singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Laura_Critchley" title="Laura Critchley">Laura Critchley</a> commented that she had sung vocals for three songs, and said that it would not be released until 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2009, it was confirmed that Williams had written material with Guy Chambers and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a>. A spokesman said that Williams was planning to begin the recording sessions in March and that the new album would be released in late 2009. This will probably be the last Williams album released by EMI.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On his official website, Williams confirmed that he was working with producer <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Horn" title="Trevor Horn">Trevor Horn</a> on his new album, which would eventually be titled <i><a href="/wiki/Reality_Killed_the_Video_Star" title="Reality Killed the Video Star">Reality Killed the Video Star</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> a reference to the song "<a href="/wiki/Video_Killed_the_Radio_Star" title="Video Killed the Radio Star">Video Killed the Radio Star</a>" by Horn\'s former band <a href="/wiki/The_Buggles" title="The Buggles">The Buggles</a>. The album was released on 9 November 2009 in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 October 2009 Williams published a 12-track compilation album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Songbook_(Robbie_Williams_album)" title="Songbook (Robbie Williams album)">Songbook</a></i>, as a free CD for the newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mail_on_Sunday" title="The Mail on Sunday">The Mail on Sunday</a></i>. The CD is a one-off album of some of his biggest hits \xe2\x80\x93 including several rare live performances.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> That same evening, Williams made his "comeback" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i> results show, performing his new single "<a href="/wiki/Bodies_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Bodies (Robbie Williams song)">Bodies</a>" for the first time live.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On 20 October 2009 Williams opened the BBC Electric Proms at the London <a href="/wiki/Roundhouse_(venue)" title="Roundhouse (venue)">RoundHouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> It was his first live concert for 3 years<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and was broadcast across 200 cinemas worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Concert_review_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concert_review-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Accompanied by a string section, horn section, full band and producer Trevor Horn, Williams performed several new tracks from <i>Reality Killed the Video Star</i> and older tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-Concert_review_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concert_review-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Reality Killed the Video Star</i> was previewed in the UK on the <a href="/wiki/Spotify" title="Spotify">Spotify</a> music streaming service on 6 November 2009, and official released on 9 November.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In a high-profile chart battle, Williams\' album was pitted against <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (UK)">X Factor</a></i> 2008 runners-up <a href="/wiki/JLS" title="JLS">JLS</a> who released their <a href="/wiki/JLS_(album)" title="JLS (album)">debut album</a> the same day. JLS beat Williams to the number one spot by 1500 sales. The album was also released in the United States (Williams\' first album to be released there since 2002\'s <i>Escapology</i>). In late November 2009, Williams travelled to Australia to perform at the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Music_Awards_of_2009" title="ARIA Music Awards of 2009">ARIA Music Awards of 2009</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932012:_In_and_Out_of_Consciousness_and_Take_the_Crown"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010\xe2\x80\x932012:_In_and_Out_of_Consciousness_and_Take_the_Crown">2010\xe2\x80\x932012: <i>In and Out of Consciousness</i> and <i>Take the Crown</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/In_and_Out_of_Consciousness:_Greatest_Hits_1990%E2%80%932010" title="In and Out of Consciousness: Greatest Hits 1990\xe2\x80\x932010">In and Out of Consciousness: Greatest Hits 1990\xe2\x80\x932010</a> and <a href="/wiki/Take_the_Crown_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Take the Crown (album)">Take the Crown (album)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbiein2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Robbiein2009.jpg/170px-Robbiein2009.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Robbiein2009.jpg/255px-Robbiein2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Robbiein2009.jpg/340px-Robbiein2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbiein2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams performing at the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Super_Dome" title="Sydney Super Dome">Sydney Super Dome</a> in 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>In October 2010, Williams released his second greatest hits album, <i><a href="/wiki/In_and_Out_of_Consciousness:_The_Greatest_Hits_1990%E2%80%932010" class="mw-redirect" title="In and Out of Consciousness: The Greatest Hits 1990\xe2\x80\x932010">In and Out of Consciousness: The Greatest Hits 1990\xe2\x80\x932010</a></i>, to celebrate 20 years as a performing artist.<sup id="cite_ref-NewAlbum_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewAlbum-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> A single, "<a href="/wiki/Shame_(Robbie_Williams_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shame (Robbie Williams song)">Shame</a>", was also released, which was written and sung by Williams and Barlow.<sup id="cite_ref-NewAlbum_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewAlbum-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 October 2011 Williams signed with <a href="/wiki/Island_Records" title="Island Records">Island Records</a> (<a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music</a>), following his departure from his previous record label EMI in 2010. He said in a statement, "I\'m really thrilled to be joining the Universal family at what I think is the most exciting time in my career."<sup id="cite_ref-newalbum_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newalbum-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Williams was the opening act at the <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Jubilee_Concert" title="Diamond Jubilee Concert">Diamond Jubilee Concert</a>, which was co-organised by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Barlow" title="Gary Barlow">Gary Barlow</a>, held outside <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> on 4 June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> During the end of August his official website began a countdown to the release of information regarding his latest solo material, with an image of his face and his mind unveiled daily as the countdown expired.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Titled <i><a href="/wiki/Take_the_Crown_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Take the Crown (album)">Take the Crown</a></i>, the album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> making it Williams\' tenth number one album. It also marked the second time that Williams had a number one single ("Candy") and album at the same time on the chart. The first time was in 2001 when "<a href="/wiki/Somethin%27_Stupid" title="Somethin&#39; Stupid">Somethin\' Stupid</a>" and <i><a href="/wiki/Swing_When_You%27re_Winning" title="Swing When You&#39;re Winning">Swing When You\'re Winning</a></i> were number one on the singles and albums chart respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The album\'s lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Candy_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Candy (Robbie Williams song)">Candy</a>", premiered on 10 September 2012 and was released on 11 September in most countries and 29 October in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In the UK, "Candy" became Williams\' first number one single since "<a href="/wiki/Radio_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Radio (Robbie Williams song)">Radio</a>" (2004) and his seventh solo number one single. In its first week the song has sold 137,000 copies becoming the fastest-selling male artist single of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> On 26 November 2012 Williams announced a <a href="/wiki/Take_The_Crown_Stadium_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Take The Crown Stadium Tour">17 date stadium tour of Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Williams also confirmed that the support act for the tour would be <a href="/wiki/Olly_Murs" title="Olly Murs">Olly Murs</a> who also duets with him on "Kids". Universal and EMI merged in 2012, bringing Williams\' Chrysalis/Virgin recordings full circle to Universal.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932014:_Swings_Both_Ways_and_Under_the_Radar_Volume_1"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013\xe2\x80\x932014:_Swings_Both_Ways_and_Under_the_Radar_Volume_1">2013\xe2\x80\x932014: <i>Swings Both Ways</i> and <i>Under the Radar Volume 1</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Swings_Both_Ways" title="Swings Both Ways">Swings Both Ways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Under_the_Radar_Volume_1" title="Under the Radar Volume 1">Under the Radar Volume 1</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg/220px-TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg/330px-TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg/440px-TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TakeTheCrownTourStage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams on stage at the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">Etihad Stadium</a> in Manchester during the <a href="/wiki/Take_the_Crown_Stadium_Tour" title="Take the Crown Stadium Tour">Take the Crown Stadium Tour</a>, June 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>In September 2013, Williams announced a follow up to his 2001 swing album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Swings_Both_Ways" title="Swings Both Ways">Swings Both Ways</a></i> for release in November. The album features covers and original songs, whilst also including duet recordings with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bubl%C3%A9" title="Michael Bubl\xc3\xa9">Michael Bubl\xc3\xa9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olly_Murs" title="Olly Murs">Olly Murs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rufus_Wainright" class="mw-redirect" title="Rufus Wainright">Rufus Wainright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lily_Allen" title="Lily Allen">Lily Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In November 2013 Williams made a cameo appearance in the video to Murs\'s song "<a href="/wiki/Hand_on_Heart" title="Hand on Heart">Hand on Heart</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Williams released a compilation album entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Under_the_Radar_Volume_1" title="Under the Radar Volume 1">Under the Radar Volume 1</a></i> on 1 December 2014 through his website, featuring <a href="/wiki/B-sides" class="mw-redirect" title="B-sides">B-sides</a>, demos and other previously unreleased songs. An example of the latter is "Run It Wild" a song that he "once got very, very excited for" and prepared for last year\'s <i>Take the Crown</i> stadium tour.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> "[These are] loads and loads of songs that I have written that I am incredibly passionate about, I want you to hear them, otherwise they are just going to remain in my computer!"<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Williams claims that Guy Chambers \xe2\x80\x9cis not happy\xe2\x80\x9d about these songs being released online: "He thinks I am a lunatic for not putting them on an album that we have promoted with TV performances and at radio stations and a big tour," Williams said. "But I am an impetuous bugger, and I want them out now, now, now!"<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2016.E2.80.93present:_The_Heavy_Entertainment_Show.2C_Under_the_Radar_Volume_2_and_The_X_Factor"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016\xe2\x80\x93present:_The_Heavy_Entertainment_Show,_Under_the_Radar_Volume_2_and_The_X_Factor">2016\xe2\x80\x93present: <i>The Heavy Entertainment Show, Under the Radar Volume 2 and The X Factor</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Heavy_Entertainment_Show" title="The Heavy Entertainment Show">The Heavy Entertainment Show</a> and <a href="/wiki/Under_the_Radar_Volume_2" title="Under the Radar Volume 2">Under the Radar Volume 2</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_Williams,_Roundhouse,_London_(Apple_Music_Festival)_(29312031654).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Robbie_Williams%2C_Roundhouse%2C_London_%28Apple_Music_Festival%29_%2829312031654%29.jpg/170px-Robbie_Williams%2C_Roundhouse%2C_London_%28Apple_Music_Festival%29_%2829312031654%29.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Robbie_Williams%2C_Roundhouse%2C_London_%28Apple_Music_Festival%29_%2829312031654%29.jpg/255px-Robbie_Williams%2C_Roundhouse%2C_London_%28Apple_Music_Festival%29_%2829312031654%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Robbie_Williams%2C_Roundhouse%2C_London_%28Apple_Music_Festival%29_%2829312031654%29.jpg/340px-Robbie_Williams%2C_Roundhouse%2C_London_%28Apple_Music_Festival%29_%2829312031654%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="4608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robbie_Williams,_Roundhouse,_London_(Apple_Music_Festival)_(29312031654).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams performing at the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music_Festival" title="Apple Music Festival">Apple Music Festival</a> in London, 25 September 2016</div></div></div>\n<p>In May 2016, it was announced that Williams had signed a recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Music Entertainment">Sony Music</a>. In a statement, Williams said: "They\xe2\x80\x99re [Sony Music] inspired, I\xe2\x80\x99m inspired. I\xe2\x80\x99m more ready than I ever have been and I\xe2\x80\x99m totally convinced I\xe2\x80\x99m in the right place. I look forward to working on this album, which is an album I\xe2\x80\x99m immensely proud of, in this exciting new partnership with Sony Music."<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Heavy_Entertainment_Show" title="The Heavy Entertainment Show">The Heavy Entertainment Show</a></i> became his <a href="/wiki/List_of_artists_by_number_of_UK_Albums_Chart_number_ones" title="List of artists by number of UK Albums Chart number ones">12th UK number-one album</a>, putting him level with <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In July 2017, Williams announced a new album, <i><a href="/wiki/Under_the_Radar_Volume_2" title="Under the Radar Volume 2">Under the Radar Volume 2</a></i>, which was released in November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sdm_4486.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Sdm_4486.jpg/220px-Sdm_4486.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Sdm_4486.jpg/330px-Sdm_4486.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Sdm_4486.jpg/440px-Sdm_4486.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sdm_4486.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams performing at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_opening_ceremony" title="2018 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony">2018 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony</a> in Moscow, Russia, 14 June 2018</div></div></div>\n<p>On 14 June 2018, Williams performed at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_opening_ceremony" title="2018 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony">2018 FIFA World Cup opening ceremony</a> held at the <a href="/wiki/Luzhniki_Stadium" title="Luzhniki Stadium">Luzhniki Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Cup_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Cup-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Williams sang \n\xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Entertain_You_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Let Me Entertain You (Robbie Williams song)">Let Me Entertain You</a>\xe2\x80\x9d and \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Feel_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Feel (Robbie Williams song)">Feel</a>\xe2\x80\x9d before he performed a duet of \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Angels_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="Angels (Robbie Williams song)">Angels</a>\xe2\x80\x9d with Russian soprano <a href="/wiki/Aida_Garifullina" title="Aida Garifullina">Aida Garifullina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Cup_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Cup-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Williams then performed an encore with \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Rock_DJ" title="Rock DJ">Rock DJ</a>\xe2\x80\x9d, during which he gave <a href="/wiki/The_finger" title="The finger">the finger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_apologises_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_apologises-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> in the U.S. apologised for the incident which they had broadcast live.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_apologises_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_apologises-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The incident was not shown on <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> in the UK who had cut away prior to the encore.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_apologises_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_apologises-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Williams appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/This_Morning_(TV_programme)" title="This Morning (TV programme)">This Morning</a></i> on 19 June and explained what happened, \xe2\x80\x9cIt was one minute to kick off, I was under a lot of pressure, because there was one minute left and I didn\'t know how I was going to do half a minute, so I just did a one-minute countdown [using his middle finger].\xe2\x80\x9d Asked by presenter <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Schofield" title="Phillip Schofield">Phillip Schofield</a> whether he regrets it, he said: "Yeah, of course, yeah. I cannot trust me. I don\'t know what I\'m going to do at any time. There\'s no, sort of, plan. The plan was, sing in key, don\'t fall over. That was the plan and 99% of the plan, I pulled off.\xe2\x80\x9d When asked did the idea just enter his head he responded, \xe2\x80\x9cNothing actually pops into my head. There\'s a block between me and sense... then something happens and then five minutes later, I\'m like, \'Did I? Yeah, I did, didn\'t I?\xe2\x80\x9d.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 July 2018, Williams along with his wife, and <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a> star <a href="/wiki/Louis_Tomlinson" title="Louis Tomlinson">Louis Tomlinson</a>, were announced as the new judges on the <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_series_15)" title="The X Factor (UK series 15)">fifteenth series</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_TV_series)" title="The X Factor (UK TV series)">The X Factor</a></i> in the UK, joining <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>, with the four also joined by <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Osbourne" title="Sharon Osbourne">Sharon Osbourne</a> on the live shows.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_projects">Other projects</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaborations">Collaborations</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robb_Queen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Robb_Queen.jpg/170px-Robb_Queen.jpg" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Robb_Queen.jpg/255px-Robb_Queen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Robb_Queen.jpg/340px-Robb_Queen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="697" data-file-height="812" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robb_Queen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Williams on stage in Poland in 2015 performing "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>". He collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> in recording \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>" for the 2001 film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Knight%27s_Tale" title="A Knight&#39;s Tale">A Knight\'s Tale</a></i></div></div></div>\n<p>Robbie Williams collaborated with Australian pop star <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a> on the song "<a href="/wiki/Kids_(Robbie_Williams_and_Kylie_Minogue_song)" title="Kids (Robbie Williams and Kylie Minogue song)">Kids</a>". The single peaked at number 2 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> in 2000 and was later selected to be part of the <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Grand_Theft_Auto_V" title="Music of Grand Theft Auto V">music of <i>Grand Theft Auto V</i></a>. Williams also collaborated with Australian film star <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman" title="Nicole Kidman">Nicole Kidman</a> on a cover of <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Sinatra" title="Nancy Sinatra">Nancy Sinatra</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Somethin%27_Stupid" title="Somethin&#39; Stupid">Somethin\' Stupid</a>". The single reached number 1 on the UK Singles Chart in 2001. His single "<a href="/wiki/No_Regrets_(Robbie_Williams_song)" title="No Regrets (Robbie Williams song)">No Regrets</a>" featured Neil Tennant, and Neil Hannon on backing vocals. In 2001, Williams recorded "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> for the 2001 medieval adventure film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Knight%27s_Tale" title="A Knight&#39;s Tale">A Knight\'s Tale</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002, Williams appeared on the track "<a href="/wiki/My_Culture" title="My Culture">My Culture</a>" on the <i><a href="/wiki/1_Giant_Leap" title="1 Giant Leap">1 Giant Leap</a></i> album, alongside rapper <a href="/wiki/Maxi_Jazz" title="Maxi Jazz">Maxi Jazz</a> (which features lyrics from the hidden track "Hello Sir" from <i><a href="/wiki/Life_thru_a_Lens" title="Life thru a Lens">Life thru a Lens</a></i>). Williams also features on a double CD titled <i>Concrete</i> which was released on the same day as <i>Rudebox</i>. The CD features a concert recorded for the BBC featuring the Pet Shop Boys and Williams singing their classic hit "Jealousy". Their joint effort, "<a href="/wiki/She%27s_Madonna" title="She&#39;s Madonna">She\'s Madonna</a>", was released as a single in March 2007. On 13 August 2007, a <a href="/wiki/Dean_Martin" title="Dean Martin">Dean Martin</a> duets album was released, on which Williams sings "<a href="/wiki/Please_Don%27t_Talk_About_Me_When_I%27m_Gone" title="Please Don&#39;t Talk About Me When I&#39;m Gone">Please Don\'t Talk About Me When I\'m Gone</a>".\n</p><p>In 2010 he announced the release of "<a href="/wiki/Shame_(Robbie_Williams_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shame (Robbie Williams song)">Shame</a>", a duet with Take That lead singer songwriter <a href="/wiki/Gary_Barlow" title="Gary Barlow">Gary Barlow</a>, as the first single from his greatest hits collection, <i><a href="/wiki/In_and_Out_of_Consciousness:_The_Greatest_Hits_1990%E2%80%932010" class="mw-redirect" title="In and Out of Consciousness: The Greatest Hits 1990\xe2\x80\x932010">In and Out of Consciousness: The Greatest Hits 1990\xe2\x80\x932010</a></i>, which was certified silver in the UK and charted in 19 countries worldwide. In 2010, Williams and comedian/actor <a href="/wiki/Russell_Brand" title="Russell Brand">Russell Brand</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Frank_Skinner" title="Frank Skinner">Frank Skinner</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Baddiel" title="David Baddiel">David Baddiel</a> and singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Ian_Broudie" title="Ian Broudie">Ian Broudie</a> (of <a href="/wiki/The_Lightning_Seeds" title="The Lightning Seeds">The Lightning Seeds</a>), under the name "The Squad", recorded a new version of \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Three_Lions" title="Three Lions">Three Lions</a>\xe2\x80\x9d, the England football team\xe2\x80\x99s song, for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Williams recorded a duet with Mexican recording artist <a href="/wiki/Thal%C3%ADa" title="Thal\xc3\xada">Thal\xc3\xada</a> for the Spanish song "Te quiero dijiste (Mu\xc3\xb1equita linda)", included on her album <i><a href="/wiki/Hab%C3%ADtame_Siempre" title="Hab\xc3\xadtame Siempre">Hab\xc3\xadtame Siempre</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_work">Other work</span></h3>\n<p>In 2005 Williams provided the voice of Dougal in the <a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Roundabout_(film)" title="The Magic Roundabout (film)">film adaption</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Roundabout_(film)" title="The Magic Roundabout (film)">The Magic Roundabou</a>t</i> On 26 August 2010, it was announced Williams would become a guest vocal coach on the ninth series of German reality television show <i><a href="/wiki/Popstars:_Girls_forever" title="Popstars: Girls forever">Popstars: Girls forever</a></i> to teach candidates for a girl group.<sup id="cite_ref-williamspopstars_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-williamspopstars-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 September 2010, Williams released his second book called <i>You Know Me</i> in collaboration with Chris Heath. The book features a collection of photographs of Williams from the past 20 years of his career and discussion of them by Williams as transcribed by Heath.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Williams launched a radio show titled <i>Radio Rudebox</i> on 6 October 2011 where he played music and interviewed Gary Barlow.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>\n<p>Williams recorded the song \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Only_Us" title="It&#39;s Only Us">It\'s Only Us</a>\xe2\x80\x9d as the theme for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_(video_game_series)" title="FIFA (video game series)"><i>FIFA</i></a> video game <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_2000" title="FIFA 2000">FIFA 2000</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-IGNPS_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGNPS-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> As part of the agreement to license the track <a href="/wiki/EA_Sports" title="EA Sports">EA Sports</a> included <a href="/wiki/Port_Vale_F.C." title="Port Vale F.C.">Port Vale</a>, the football club Williams supports, in the game, despite only being in the third tier of the English football league system.<sup id="cite_ref-IGNPS_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGNPS-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Williams features in his own karaoke video game, <i><a href="/wiki/We_Sing_Robbie_Williams" title="We Sing Robbie Williams">We Sing Robbie Williams</a></i> which was released on 12 November 2010 by Nordic Games Publishing AB.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Los_Angeles_Vale_F.C.">Los Angeles Vale F.C.</span></h3>\n<p>In 2005, Williams founded a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> team called LA Vale FC. Williams formed the club with other celebrity friends after building his own soccer pitch at his home in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The club was named after Williams\' hometown club, <a href="/wiki/Port_Vale_F.C." title="Port Vale F.C.">Port Vale</a>, and its logo was very similar.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The club supposedly was disbanded in 2007, reportedly after Williams discovered two players had swindled him out of \xc2\xa3200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Farrell_clothing">Farrell clothing</span></h3>\n<p>In 2011, Williams announced he was working with <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jones_(entrepreneur)" title="Peter Jones (entrepreneur)">entrepreneur Peter Jones</a> in developing a clothing line called Farrell in honour of his grandfather Jack Farrell.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Although the business had filed for bankruptcy, it was later relaunched in 2014 with support of clothing company <a href="/wiki/Primark" title="Primark">Primark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_theatre">Musical theatre</span></h3>\n<p>Williams and Guy Chambers will provide the music and lyrics (with a book by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ravenhill" title="Mark Ravenhill">Mark Ravenhill</a>) for the upcoming stage adaptation of <a href="/wiki/David_Walliams" title="David Walliams">David Walliams\'</a> children\'s book <a href="/wiki/The_Boy_in_the_Dress_(musical)" title="The Boy in the Dress (musical)"><i>The Boy in the Dress</i></a>. The musical will be produced by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Shakespeare_Company" title="Royal Shakespeare Company">Royal Shakespeare Company</a> where it will premiere in <a href="/wiki/Stratford-upon-Avon" title="Stratford-upon-Avon">Stratford-upon-Avon</a> for the Christmas 2019 season (before an anticipated transfer to <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">London\'s West End</a> in 2020).<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estatua_de_RW,_Madame_Tussauds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Estatua_de_RW%2C_Madame_Tussauds.jpg/170px-Estatua_de_RW%2C_Madame_Tussauds.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Estatua_de_RW%2C_Madame_Tussauds.jpg/255px-Estatua_de_RW%2C_Madame_Tussauds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Estatua_de_RW%2C_Madame_Tussauds.jpg/340px-Estatua_de_RW%2C_Madame_Tussauds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estatua_de_RW,_Madame_Tussauds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wax statue of Williams at <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> in London</div></div></div>\n<p>It has been claimed that Williams has sold more albums in the UK than any other British solo artist in history and has won more BRIT Awards than any other artist to date.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> His records sales stands at over 77 million worldwide, making him one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling artists of all time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reporter_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reporter-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Williams was entered in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="The Guinness Book of World Records">The Guinness Book of World Records</a></i> when, after he announced his World Tour for 2006, 1.6&#160;million tickets were sold in one day.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:23%;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s his <a href="/wiki/Self-deprecating" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-deprecating">self-deprecating</a> sense of humour \xe2\x80\x94 in person and in his lyrics \xe2\x80\x94 that helps explain his wide appeal in Australia. Perhaps only Pink and Ed Sheeran have such a wide mix of demographics at their concerts; that\xe2\x80\x99s why Williams will play to nearly 60,000 people in Victoria alone.\xe2\x80\x9d</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Cameron Adams on the appeal of Williams.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a
